For each topic, we lay out the available partitions in numeric order\\n44:  * and the consumers in lexicographic order. We then divide the number of partitions by the total number of\\n45:  * consumers to determine the number of partitions to assign to each consumer. If it does not evenly\\n46:  * divide, then the first few consumers will have one extra partition.\\n47:  *\\n48:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and\\n49:  * <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>,\\n50:  * <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n51:  *\\n52:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n53:  * <ul>\\n54:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n55:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code></li>\\n56:  * </ul>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\\n59:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n60:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C2</code>.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n63:  * <ul>\\n64:  * <li><code>C3 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1])</code>\\n65:  * <li><code>C2 (was C1): [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n66:  * </ul>\\n67:  *\\n68:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\\n69:  * can be avoided by setting the group.instance.id.\\n70:  * Consumers will have individual instance ids <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>. As long as\\n71:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\\n72:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\\n73:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\\n74:  *\\n75:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n76:  * <ul>\\n77:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code>\\n78:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n79:  * </ul>\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Rack-aware assignment is used if both consumer and partition replica racks are available and\\n82:  * some partitions have replicas only on a subset of racks. We attempt to match consumer racks with\\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\\n89:  * <p>\\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\\n95:  * </p>\\n96:  */\\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \\\"range\\\";\\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\\n100: \\n101:     @Override\\n102:     public String name() {\\n103:         return RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME;\\n104:     }\\n105: \\n106:     private Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic(Map<String, Subscription> consumerMetadata) {\\n107:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> topicToConsumers = new HashMap<>();\\n108:         consumerMetadata.forEach((consumerId, subscription) -> {\\n109:             MemberInfo memberInfo = new MemberInfo(consumerId, subscription.groupInstanceId(), subscription.rackId());\\n110:             subscription.topics().forEach(topic -> put(topicToConsumers, topic, memberInfo));\\n111:         });\\n112:         return topicToConsumers;\\n113:     }\\n114: \\n115:     /**\\n116:      * Performs range assignment of the specified partitions for the consumers with the provided subscriptions.\\n117:      * If rack-awareness is enabled for one or more consumers, we perform rack-aware assignment first to assign\\n118:      * the subset of partitions that can be aligned on racks, while retaining the same co-partitioning and\\n119:      * per-topic balancing guarantees as non-rack-aware range assignment. The remaining partitions are assigned\\n120:      * using standard non-rack-aware range assignment logic, which may result in mis-aligned racks.\\n121:      */\\n122:     @Override\\n123:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignPartitions(Map<String, List<PartitionInfo>> partitionsPerTopic,\\n124:                                                               Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\\n125:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic = consumersPerTopic(subscriptions);\\n126:         Map<String, String> consumerRacks = consumerRacks(subscriptions);\\n127:         List<TopicAssignmentState> topicAssignmentStates = partitionsPerTopic.entrySet().stream()\\n128:                 .filter(e -> !e.getValue().isEmpty())\\n129:                 .map(e -> new TopicAssignmentState(e.getKey(), e.getValue(), consumersPerTopic.get(e.getKey()), consumerRacks))\\n130:                 .collect(Collectors.toList());\\n131: \\n132:         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment = new HashMap<>();\\n133:         subscriptions.keySet().forEach(memberId -> assignment.put(memberId, new ArrayList<>()));\\n134: \\n135:         boolean useRackAware = topicAssignmentStates.stream().anyMatch(t -> t.needsRackAwareAssignment);\\n136:         if (useRackAware)\\n137:             assignWithRackMatching(topicAssignmentStates, assignment);\\n138: \\n139:         topicAssignmentStates.forEach(t -> assignRanges(t, (c, tp) -> true, assignment));\\n140: \\n141:         if (useRackAware)\\n142:             assignment.values().forEach(list -> list.sort(PARTITION_COMPARATOR));\\n143:         return assignment;\\n144:     }\\n145: \\n146:     // This method is not used, but retained for compatibility with any custom assignors that extend this class.\\n147:     @Override\\n148:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assign(Map<String, Integer> partitionsPerTopic,\\n149:                                                     Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\\n150:         return              BiFunction<String, TopicPartition, Boolean> mayAssign,\\n155:                               Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\\n156:         for (String consumer : assignmentState.consumers.keySet()) {\\n157:             if (assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.isEmpty())\\n158:                 break;\\n159:             List<TopicPartition> assignablePartitions = assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.stream()\\n160:                     .filter(tp -> mayAssign.apply(consumer, tp))\\n161:                     .limit(assignmentState.maxAssignable(consumer))\\n162:                     .collect(Collectors.toList());\\n163:             if (assignablePartitions.isEmpty())\\n164:                 continue;\\n165: \\n166:             assign(consumer, assignablePartitions, assignmentState, assignment);\\n167:         }\\n168:     }\\n169: \\n170:     private void assignWithRackMatching(Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\\n171:                                         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\\n172: \\n173:         assignmentStates.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.consumers)).forEach((consumers, states) ->\\n174:             states.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.partitionRacks.size())).forEach((numPartitions, coPartitionedStates) -> {\\n175:                 if (coPartitionedStates.size() > 1)\\n176:                     assignCoPartitionedWithRackMatching(consumers, numPartitions, coPartitionedStates, assignment);\\n177:                 else {\\n178:                     TopicAssignmentState state = coPartitionedStates.get(0);\\n179:                     if (state.needsRackAwareAssignment)\\n180:                         assignRanges(state, state::racksMatch, assignment);\\n181:                 }\\n182:             })\\n183:         );\\n184:     }\\n185: \\n186:     private void assignCoPartitionedWithRackMatching(LinkedHashMap<String, Optional<String>> consumers,\\n187:                                                      int numPartitions,\\n188:                                                      Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\\n189:                                                      Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\\n190: \\n191:         Set<String> remainingConsumers = new LinkedHashSet<>(consumers.keySet());\\n192:         for (int i = 0; i < numPartitions; i++) {\\n193:             int p = i;\\n194: \\n195:             Optional<String> matchingConsumer = remainingConsumers.stream()\\n196:                     .filter(c -> assignmentStates.stream().allMatch(t -> t.racksMatch(c, new TopicPartition(t.topic, p)) && t.maxAssignable(c) > 0))\\n197:                     .findFirst();\\n198:             if (matchingConsumer.isPresent()) {\\n199:                 String consumer = matchingConsumer.get();\\n200:                 assignmentStates.forEach(t -> assign(consumer, Collections.singletonList(new TopicPartition(t.topic, p)), t, assignment));\\n201: \\n202:                 if (assignmentStates.stream().noneMatch(t -> t.maxAssignable(consumer) > 0)) {\\n203:                     remainingConsumers.remove(consumer);\\n204:                     if (remainingConsumers.isEmpty())\\n205:                         break;\\n206:                 }\\n207:             }\\n208:         }\\n209:     }\\n210: \\n211:     private void assign(String consumer, List<TopicPartition> partitions, TopicAssignmentState assignmentState, Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\\n212:         assignment.get(consumer).addAll(partitions);\\n213:         assignmentState.onAssigned(consumer, partitions);\\n214:     }\\n215: \\n216:     private Map<String, String> consumerRacks(Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\\n217:         Map<String, String> consumerRacks = new HashMap<>(subscriptions.size());\\n218:         subscriptions.forEach((memberId, subscription) ->\\n219:                 subscription.rackId().filter(r -> !r.isEmpty()).ifPresent(rackId -> consumerRacks.put(memberId, rackId)));\\n220:         return consumerRacks;\\n221:     }\\n222: \\n223:     private class For each topic, we lay out the available partitions in numeric order\\n44:  * and the consumers in lexicographic order. We then divide the number of partitions by the total number of\\n45:  * consumers to determine the number of partitions to assign to each consumer. If it does not evenly\\n46:  * divide, then the first few consumers will have one extra partition.\\n47:  *\\n48:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and\\n49:  * <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>,\\n50:  * <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n51:  *\\n52:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n53:  * <ul>\\n54:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n55:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code></li>\\n56:  * </ul>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\\n59:  * For the above example, after one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n60:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C2</code>.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n63:  * <ul>\\n64:  * <li><code>C3 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1])</code>\\n65:  * <li><code>C2 (was C1): [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n66:  * </ul>\\n67:  *\\n68:  * The assignment change was caused by the change of <code>member.id</code> relative order, and\\n69:  * can be avoided by setting the group.instance.id.\\n70:  * Consumers will have individual instance ids <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>. As long as\\n71:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\\n72:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\\n73:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\\n74:  *\\n75:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n76:  * <ul>\\n77:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t0p1, t1p0, t1p1]</code>\\n78:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n79:  * </ul>\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Rack-aware assignment is used if both consumer and partition replica racks are available and\\n82:  * some partitions have replicas only on a subset of racks. We attempt to match consumer racks with\\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\\n89:  * <p>\\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\\n95:  * </p>\\n96:  */\\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \\\"range\\\";\\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\\n100: \\n101:     @Override\\n102:     public String name() {\\n103:         return RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME;\\n104:     }\\n105: \\n106:     private Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic(Map<String, Subscription> consumerMetadata) {\\n107:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> topicToConsumers = new HashMap<>();\\n108:         consumerMetadata.forEach((consumerId, subscription) -> {\\n109:             MemberInfo memberInfo = new MemberInfo(consumerId, subscription.groupInstanceId(), subscription.rackId());\\n110:             subscription.topics().forEach(topic -> put(topicToConsumers, topic, memberInfo));\\n111:         });\\n112:         return topicToConsumers;\\n113:     }\\n114: \\n115:     /**\\n116:      * Performs range assignment of the specified partitions for the consumers with the provided subscriptions.\\n117:      * If rack-awareness is enabled for one or more consumers, we perform rack-aware assignment first to assign\\n118:      * the subset of partitions that can be aligned on racks, while retaining the same co-partitioning and\\n119:      * per-topic balancing guarantees as non-rack-aware range assignment. The remaining partitions are assigned\\n120:      * using standard non-rack-aware range assignment logic, which may result in mis-aligned racks.\\n121:      */\\n122:     @Override\\n123:     public We attempt to match consumer racks with\n83:  * partition replica racks on a best-effort basis, prioritizing balanced assignment over rack alignment.\n84:  * Topics with equal partition count and same set of subscribers guarantee co-partitioning by prioritizing\n85:  * co-partitioning over rack alignment. In this case, aligning partition replicas of these topics on the\n86:  * same racks will improve locality for consumers. For example, if partitions 0 of all topics have a replica\n87:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 on rack 'b' etc., partition 0 of all topics can be assigned to a consumer\n88:  * on rack 'a', partition 1 to a consumer on rack 'b' and so on.\n89:  * <p>\n90:  * Note that rack-aware assignment currently takes all replicas into account, including any offline replicas\n91:  * and replicas that are not in the ISR. This is based on the assumption that these replicas are likely\n92:  * to join the ISR relatively soon. Since consumers don't rebalance on ISR change, this avoids unnecessary\n93:  * cross-rack traffic for long durations after replicas rejoin the ISR. In the future, we may consider\n94:  * rebalancing when replicas are added or removed to improve consumer rack alignment.\n95:  * </p>\n96:  */\n97: public class RangeAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\n98:     public static final String RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME = \"range\";\n99:     private static final TopicPartitionComparator PARTITION_COMPARATOR = new TopicPartitionComparator();\n100: \n101:     @Override\n102:     public String name() {\n103:         return RANGE_ASSIGNOR_NAME;\n104:     }\n105: \n106:     private Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic(Map<String, Subscription> consumerMetadata) {\n107:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> topicToConsumers = new HashMap<>();\n108:         consumerMetadata.forEach((consumerId, subscription) -> {\n109:             MemberInfo memberInfo = new MemberInfo(consumerId, subscription.groupInstanceId(), subscription.rackId());\n110:             subscription.topics().forEach(topic -> put(topicToConsumers, topic, memberInfo));\n111:         });\n112:         return topicToConsumers;\n113:     }\n114: \n115:     /**\n116:      * Performs range assignment of the specified partitions for the consumers with the provided subscriptions.\n117:      * If rack-awareness is enabled for one or more consumers, we perform rack-aware assignment first to assign\n118:      * the subset of partitions that can be aligned on racks, while retaining the same co-partitioning and\n119:      * per-topic balancing guarantees as non-rack-aware range assignment. The remaining partitions are assigned\n120:      * using standard non-rack-aware range assignment logic, which may result in mis-aligned racks.\n121:      */\n122:     @Override\n123:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignPartitions(Map<String, List<PartitionInfo>> partitionsPerTopic,\n124:                                                               Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\n125:         Map<String, List<MemberInfo>> consumersPerTopic = consumersPerTopic(subscriptions);\n126:         Map<String, String> consumerRacks = consumerRacks(subscriptions);\n127:         List<TopicAssignmentState> topicAssignmentStates = partitionsPerTopic.entrySet().stream()\n128:                 .filter(e -> !e.getValue().isEmpty())\n129:                 .map(e -> new TopicAssignmentState(e.getKey(), e.getValue(), consumersPerTopic.get(e.getKey()), consumerRacks))\n130:                 .collect(Collectors.toList());\n131: \n132:         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment = new HashMap<>();\n133:         subscriptions.keySet().forEach(memberId -> assignment.put(memberId, new ArrayList<>()));\n134: \n135:         boolean useRackAware = topicAssignmentStates.stream().anyMatch(t -> t.needsRackAwareAssignment);\n136:         if (useRackAware)\n137:             assignWithRackMatching(topicAssignmentStates, assignment);\n138: \n139:         topicAssignmentStates.forEach(t -> assignRanges(t, (c, tp) -> true, assignment));\n140: \n141:         if (useRackAware)\n142:             assignment.values().forEach(list -> list.sort(PARTITION_COMPARATOR));\n143:         return assignment;\n144:     }\n145: \n146:     // This method is not used, but retained for compatibility with any custom assignors that extend this class.\n147:     @Override\n148:     public Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assign(Map<String, Integer> partitionsPerTopic,\n149:                                                     Map<String, Subscription> subscriptions) {\n150:         return assignPartitions(partitionInfosWithoutRacks(partitionsPerTopic), subscriptions);\n151:     }\n152: \n153:     private void assignRanges(TopicAssignmentState assignmentState,\n154:                               BiFunction<String, TopicPartition, Boolean> mayAssign,\n155:                               Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n156:         for (String consumer : assignmentState.consumers.keySet()) {\n157:             if (assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.isEmpty())\n158:                 break;\n159:             List<TopicPartition> assignablePartitions = assignmentState.unassignedPartitions.stream()\n160:                     .filter(tp -> mayAssign.apply(consumer, tp))\n161:                     .limit(assignmentState.maxAssignable(consumer))\n162:                     .collect(Collectors.toList());\n163:             if (assignablePartitions.isEmpty())\n164:                 continue;\n165: \n166:             assign(consumer, assignablePartitions, assignmentState, assignment);\n167:         }\n168:     }\n169: \n170:     private void assignWithRackMatching(Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\n171:                                         Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n172: \n173:         assignmentStates.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.consumers)).forEach((consumers, states) ->\n174:             states.stream().collect(Collectors.groupingBy(t -> t.partitionRacks.size())).forEach((numPartitions, coPartitionedStates) -> {\n175:                 if (coPartitionedStates.size() > 1)\n176:                     assignCoPartitionedWithRackMatching(consumers, numPartitions, coPartitionedStates, assignment);\n177:                 else {\n178:                     TopicAssignmentState state = coPartitionedStates.get(0);\n179:                     if (state.needsRackAwareAssignment)\n180:                         assignRanges(state, state::racksMatch, assignment);\n181:                 }\n182:             })\n183:         );\n184:     }\n185: \n186:     private void assignCoPartitionedWithRackMatching(LinkedHashMap<String, Optional<String>> consumers,\n187:                                                      int numPartitions,\n188:                                                      Collection<TopicAssignmentState> assignmentStates,\n189:                                                      Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n190: \n191:         Set<String> remainingConsumers = new LinkedHashSet<>(consumers.keySet());\n192:         for (int i = 0; i < numPartitions; i++) {\n193:             int p = i;\n194: \n195:             Optional<String> matchingConsumer = remainingConsumers.stream()\n196:                     .filter(c ->    }\n210: \n211:     private void assign(String consumer, List<TopicPartition> partitions, TopicAssignmentState assignmentState, Map<String, List<TopicPartition>> assignment) {\n212: TopicAssignmentState {\n224:         private final String topic;\n225:         private final LinkedHashMap<String, Optional<String>> consumers;\n226:         private final boolean needsRackAwareAssignment;\n227:         private final Map<TopicPartition, Set<String>> partitionRacks;\n228: \n229:         private final Set<TopicPartition> unassignedPartitions;\n230: public TopicAssignmentState(String topic, List<PartitionInfo> partitionInfos, List<MemberInfo> membersOrNull, Map<String, String> consumerRacks) {\n235:             this.topic = topic;\n236:             List<MemberInfo> members = membersOrNull == null ? 0 : partitionInfos.size() / consumers.size();\n245:             remainingConsumersWithExtraPartition = consumers.isEmpty() ? 0 : partitionInfos.size() % consumers.size();\n246: \n247:             Set<String> allConsumerRacks = new HashSet<>();\n248:             Set<String> allPartitionRacks = new HashSet<>();\n249:             members.stream().map(m -> m.memberId).filter(consumerRacks::containsKey)\n250:                     .forEach(memberId -> allConsumerRacks.add(consumerRacks.get(memberId)));\n251:             if (!allConsumerRacks.isEmpty()) {\n252:                 partitionRacks = new HashMap<>(partitionInfos.size());\n253:                 partitionInfos.forEach(p -> {\n254:                     TopicPartition tp = new TopicPartition(p.topic(), p.partition());\n255:                     Set<String> racks = Arrays.stream(p.replicas())\n256:                             .map(Node::rack)\n257:                             .filter(Objects::nonNull)\n258:                             .collect(Collectors.toSet());\n259:                     partitionRacks.put(tp, racks);\n260:                     allPartitionRacks.addAll(racks);\n261:                 });\n262:             } else {\n263:                 partitionRacks = Collections.emptyMap();\n264:             }\n265: \n266:             needsRackAwareAssignment = useRackAwareAssignment(allConsumerRacks, allPartitionRacks, partitionRacks);\n267:         }\n268: \n269:         boolean racksMatch(String consumer, TopicPartition tp) {\n270:             Optional<String> consumerRack = consumers.get(consumer);\n271:             Set<String> replicaRacks = partitionRacks.get(tp);\n272:             return consumerRack.isEmpty() || (replicaRacks != null && replicaRacks.contains(consumerRack.get()));\n273:         }\n274: \n275:         int maxAssignable(String consumer) {\n276:             int maxForConsumer = numPartitionsPerConsumer + (remainingConsumersWithExtraPartition > 0 ? 1 : 0) - numAssignedByConsumer.get(consumer);\n277:             return Math.max(0, maxForConsumer);\n278:         }\n279: \n280:         void onAssigned(String consumer, List<TopicPartition> newlyAssignedPartitions) {\n281:             int numAssigned = numAssignedByConsumer.compute(consumer, (c, n) -> n + newlyAssignedPartitions.size());\n282:             if (numAssigned > numPartitionsPerConsumer)\n283:                 remainingConsumersWithExtraPartition--;\n284:             unassignedPartitions.removeAll(newlyAssignedPartitions);\n285:         }\n286: \n287:         @Override\n288:         public String toString() {\n289:             return \"TopicAssignmentState(\" +\n290:                     \"topic=\" + topic +\n291:                     \", consumers=\" + consumers +\n292:                     \", partitionRacks=\" + partitionRacks +\n293:                     \", unassignedPartitions=\" + unassignedPartitions +\n294:                     \")\";\n295:         }\n296:     }\n297: }\n298: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/RangeAssignor.java"}}}

It\\n33:  * then proceeds to do a round robin assignment from partition to consumer. If the subscriptions of all consumer\\n34:  * instances are identical, then the partitions will be uniformly distributed. (i.e., the partition ownership counts\\n35:  * will be within a delta of exactly one across all consumers.)\\n36:  *\\n37:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and <code>t1</code>,\\n38:  * and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t0p2</code>,\\n39:  * <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\\n40:  *\\n41:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n42:  * <ul>\\n43:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p2, t1p1]</code>\\n44:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p0, t1p2]</code>\\n45:  * </ul>\\n46:  *\\n47:  * <p>When subscriptions differ across consumer instances, the assignment process still considers each\\n48:  * consumer instance in round robin fashion but skips over an instance if it is not subscribed to\\n49:  * the topic. Unlike the case when subscriptions are identical, this can result in imbalanced\\n50:  * assignments. For example, we have three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n51:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions, respectively.\\n52:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>, <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>.\\n53:  * <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>;\\n54:  * <code>C1</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>;\\n55:  * and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>That assignment will be:\\n58:  * <ul>\\n59:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0]</code>\\n60:  * <li><code>C1: [t1p0]</code>\\n61:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code>\\n62:  * </ul>\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\\n65:  * For example, we have three consumers with assigned <code>member.id</code> <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n66:  * two topics <code>t0</code> and <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>,\\n67:  * <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>. We choose to honor\\n68:  * the sorted order based on ephemeral <code>member.id</code>.\\n69:  *\\n70:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n71:  * <ul>\\n72:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\\n73:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p1]</code>\\n74:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n75:  * </ul>\\n76:  *\\n77:  * After one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n78:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C5</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code>, <code>C2</code> -&gt; <code>C4</code>.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n81:  * <ul>\\n82:  * <li><code>C3 (was C1): [t0p0, t1p0] (before was [t0p1, t1p1])</code>\\n83:  * <li><code>C4 (was C2): [t0p1, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n84:  * <li><code>C5 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t1p0])</code>\\n85:  * </ul>\\n86:  *\\n87:  * This issue could be mitigated by the introduction of static membership. Consumers will have individual instance ids\\n88:  * <code>I1</code>, <code>I2</code>, <code>I3</code>. As long as\\n89:  * 1. Number of members remain the same across generation\\n90:  * 2. Static members' identities persist across generation\\n91:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\\n92:  *\\n93:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n94:  * <ul>\\n95:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\\n96:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p1, We choose to honor\\n68:  * the sorted order based on ephemeral <code>member.id</code>.\\n69:  *\\n70:  * <p>The assignment will be:\\n71:  * <ul>\\n72:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\\n73:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p1]</code>\\n74:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n75:  * </ul>\\n76:  *\\n77:  * After one rolling bounce, group coordinator will attempt to assign new <code>member.id</code> towards consumers,\\n78:  * for example <code>C0</code> -&gt; <code>C5</code> <code>C1</code> -&gt; <code>C3</code>, <code>C2</code> -&gt; <code>C4</code>.\\n79:  *\\n80:  * <p>The assignment could be completely shuffled to:\\n81:  * <ul>\\n82:  * <li><code>C3 (was C1): [t0p0, t1p0] (before was [t0p1, t1p1])</code>\\n83:  * <li><code>C4 (was C2): [t0p1, t1p1] (before was [t0p2, t1p2])</code>\\n84:  * <li><code>C5 (was C0): [t0p2, t1p2] (before was [t0p0, t1p0])</code>\\n85:  * </ul>\\n86:  *\\n87:  * This issue could be mitigated by the introduction of static membership. Static members' identities persist across generation\\n91:  * 3. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\\n92:  *\\n93:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\\n94:  * <ul>\\n95:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\\n96:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p1, t1p1]</code>\\n97:  * <li><code>I2: [t0p2, t1p2]</code>\\n98:  * </ul>\\n99:  */\\n100: public class RoundRobinAssignor extends AbstractPartitionAssignor {\\n101:     public static final String It\n33:  * then proceeds to do a round robin assignment from partition to consumer. If the subscriptions of all consumer\n34:  * instances are identical, then the partitions will be uniformly distributed. (i.e., the partition ownership counts\n35:  * will be within a delta of exactly one across all consumers.)\n36:  *\n37:  * <p>For example, suppose there are two consumers <code>C0</code> and <code>C1</code>, two topics <code>t0</code> and <code>t1</code>,\n38:  * and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t0p2</code>,\n39:  * <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>.\n40:  *\n41:  * <p>The assignment will be:\n42:  * <ul>\n43:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t0p2, t1p1]</code>\n44:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t1p0, t1p2]</code>\n45:  * </ul>\n46:  *\n47:  * <p>When subscriptions differ across consumer instances, the assignment process still considers each\n48:  * consumer instance in round robin fashion but skips over an instance if it is not subscribed to\n49:  * the topic. Unlike the case when subscriptions are identical, this can result in imbalanced\n50:  * assignments. For example, we have three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n51:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions, respectively.\n52:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>, <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>.\n53:  * <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>;\n54:  * <code>C1</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>;\n55:  * and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\n56:  *\n57:  * <p>That assignment will be:\n58:  * <ul>\n59:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0]</code>\n60:  * <li><code>C1: [t1p0]</code>\n61:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code>\n62:  * </ul>\n63:  *\n64:  * Since the introduction of static membership, we could leverage <code>group.instance.id</code> to make the assignment behavior more sticky.\n65:  * For example, we have three consumers with assigned <code>member.id</code> <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n66:  * two topics <code>t0</code> and <code>t1</code>, and each topic has 3 partitions, resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>,\n67:  * <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t0p2</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, and <code>t1p2</code>. Subscription pattern doesn't change for any member\n92:  *\n93:  * <p>The assignment will always be:\n94:  * <ul>\n95:  * <li><code>I0: [t0p0, t1p0]</code>\n96:  * <li><code>I1: [t0p1, You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n8:  *\\n9:  *    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n10:  *\\n11:  * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n12:  * distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n13:  * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n14:  * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n15:  * limitations under the License.\\n16:  */\\n17: package org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer;\\n18: \\n19: import org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.internals.AbstractStickyAssignor;\\n20: import org.apache.kafka.common.TopicPartition;\\n21: import org.apache.kafka.common.protocol.types.ArrayOf;\\n22: import org.apache.kafka.common.protocol.types.Field;\\n23: import org.apache.kafka.common.protocol.types.Schema;\\n24: import org.apache.kafka.common.protocol.types.Struct;\\n25: import org.apache.kafka.common.protocol.types.Type;\\n26: import org.apache.kafka.common.utils.CollectionUtils;\\n27: \\n28: import java.nio.ByteBuffer;\\n29: import java.util.ArrayList;\\n30: import java.util.Collections;\\n31: import java.util.List;\\n32: import java.util.Map;\\n33: import java.util.Optional;\\n34: import java.util.Set;\\n35: \\n36: /**\\n37:  * <p>The sticky assignor serves two purposes. First, it guarantees an assignment that is as balanced as possible, meaning either:\\n38:  * <ul>\\n39:  * <li>the numbers of topic partitions assigned to consumers differ by at most one; or</li>\\n40:  * <li>each consumer that has 2+ fewer topic partitions than some other consumer cannot get any of those topic partitions transferred to it.</li>\\n41:  * </ul>\\n42:  * Second, it preserved as many existing assignment as possible when a reassignment occurs. This helps in saving some of the\\n43:  * overhead processing when topic partitions move from one consumer to another.</p>\\n44:  *\\n45:  * <p>Starting fresh it would work by distributing the partitions over consumers as evenly as possible. Even though this may sound similar to\\n46:  * how round robin assignor works, the second example below shows that it is not.\\n47:  * During a reassignment it would perform the reassignment in such a way that in the new assignment\\n48:  * <ol>\\n49:  * <li>topic partitions are still distributed as evenly as possible, and</li>\\n50:  * <li>topic partitions stay with their previously assigned consumers as much as possible.</li>\\n51:  * </ol>\\n52:  * Of course, the first goal above takes precedence over the second one.</p>\\n53:  *\\n54:  * <p><b>Example 1.</b> Suppose there are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n55:  * four topics <code>t0,</code> <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, <code>t3</code>, and each topic has 2 partitions,\\n56:  * resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\\n57:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t3p0</code>, <code>t3p1</code>. Each consumer is subscribed to all three topics.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * The assignment with both sticky and round robin assignors will be:\\n60:  * <ul>\\n61:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0]</code></li>\\n62:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t2p0, t3p1]</code></li>\\n63:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p0, t2p1]</code></li>\\n64:  * </ul>\\n65:  *\\n66:  * Now, let's assume <code>C1</code> is removed and a reassignment is about to happen. The round robin assignor would produce:\\n67:  * <ul>\\n68:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0, t2p0, t3p0]</code></li>\\n69:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p1, t1p1, t2p1, t3p1]</code></li>\\n70:  * </ul>\\n71:  *\\n72:  * while the sticky assignor would result in:\\n73:  * <ul>\\n74:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0, t2p0]</code></li>\\n75:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p1, t0p1, t3p1]</code></li>\\n76:  * </ul>\\n77:  * preserving all the previous assignments (unlike the round robin assignor).\\n78:  *</p>\\n79:  * <p><b>Example 2.</b> There are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n80:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions respectively.\\n81:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\\n82:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>. <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>; <code>C1</code> is subscribed to\\n83:  * <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>; and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * The round robin assignor would come up with the following assignment:\\n86:  * <ul>\\n87:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\\n88:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0]</code></li>\\n89:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n90:  * </ul>\\n91:  *\\n92:  * which is not as balanced as the assignment suggested by sticky assignor:\\n93:  * <ul>\\n94:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\\n95:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n96:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n97:  * </ul>\\n98:  *\\n99:  * Now, if consumer <code>C0</code> is removed, these two assignors would produce the following assignments.\\n100:  * Round Robin (preserves 3 partition assignments):\\n101:  * <ul>\\n102:  * <li><code>C1 [t0p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n103:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n104:  * </ul>\\n105:  *\\n106:  * Sticky (preserves 5 partition assignments):\\n107:  * <ul>\\n108:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1, t0p0]</code></li>\\n109:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n110:  * </ul>\\n111:  *</p>\\n112:  * <h3>Impact on <code>ConsumerRebalanceListener</code></h3>\\n113:  * The sticky assignment strategy can provide some optimization to those consumers that have some partition cleanup code\\n114:  * in their <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code> callback listeners. The cleanup code is placed in that callback listener\\n115:  * because the consumer has no assumption or hope of preserving any of its assigned partitions after a rebalance when it\\n116:  * is using range or round robin assignor. The listener code would look like this:\\n117:  * <pre>\\n118:  * {@code\\n119:  * class TheOldRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n120:  *\\n121:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n122:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\\n123:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\\n124:  *       cleanupState(partition);\\n125:  *     }\\n126:  *   }\\n127:  *\\n128:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n129:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\\n130:  *       initializeState(partition);\\n131:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\\n132:  *     }\\n133:  *   }\\n134:  * }\\n135:  * }\\n136:  * </pre>\\n137:  *\\n138:  * As mentioned above, one advantage of the sticky assignor is that, in general, it reduces the number of partitions that\\n139:  * actually move from one consumer to another during a reassignment. Therefore, it allows consumers to do their cleanup\\n140:  * more efficiently. Of course, they still can perform the partition cleanup in the <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code>\\n141:  * listener, but they can be more efficient and make a note of their partitions before and after the rebalance, and do the\\n142:  * cleanup after the rebalance only on the partitions they have lost (which is normally not a lot). The code snippet below\\n143:  * clarifies this point:\\n144:  * <pre>\\n145:  * {@code\\n146:  * class TheNewRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n147:  *   Collection<TopicPartition> lastAssignment = Collections.emptyList();\\n148:  *\\n149:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n150:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n151:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\\n152:  *   }\\n153:  *\\n154:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> assignment) {\\n155:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(lastAssignment, assignment))\\n156:  *       cleanupState(partition);\\n157:  *\\n158:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(assignment, lastAssignment))\\n159:  *       initializeState(partition);\\n160:  *\\n161:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: assignment)\\n162:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\\n163:  *\\n164:  *     this.lastAssignment = assignment;\\n165:  *   }\\n166:  * }\\n167:  * }\\n168:  * </pre>\\n169:  *\\n170:  * Any consumer that uses sticky assignment can leverage this listener like this:\\n171:  * <code>consumer.subscribe(topics, new TheNewRebalanceListener());</code>\\n172:  *\\n173:  * Note that you can leverage the {@link CooperativeStickyAssignor} so that only partitions which are being\\n174:  * reassigned to another consumer will be revoked. That is the preferred assignor for newer cluster. See\\n175:  * {@link ConsumerPartitionAssignor.RebalanceProtocol} for a detailed explanation of cooperative rebalancing.\\n176:  */\\n177: public class StickyAssignor extends AbstractStickyAssignor First, it guarantees an assignment that is as balanced as possible, meaning either:\\n38:  * <ul>\\n39:  * <li>the numbers of topic partitions assigned to consumers differ by at most one; or</li>\\n40:  * <li>each consumer that has 2+ fewer topic partitions than some other consumer cannot get any of those topic partitions transferred to it.</li>\\n41:  * </ul>\\n42:  * Second, it preserved as many existing assignment as possible when a reassignment occurs. This helps in saving some of the\\n43:  * overhead processing when topic partitions move from one consumer to another.</p>\\n44:  *\\n45:  * <p>Starting fresh it would work by distributing the partitions over consumers as evenly as possible. Even though this may sound similar to\\n46:  * how round robin assignor works, the second example below shows that it is not.\\n47:  * During a reassignment it would perform the reassignment in such a way that in the new assignment\\n48:  * <ol>\\n49:  * <li>topic partitions are still distributed as evenly as possible, and</li>\\n50:  * <li>topic partitions stay with their previously assigned consumers as much as possible.</li>\\n51:  * </ol>\\n52:  * Of course, the first goal above takes precedence over the second one.</p>\\n53:  *\\n54:  * <p><b>Example 1.</b> Suppose there are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n55:  * four topics <code>t0,</code> <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, <code>t3</code>, and each topic has 2 partitions,\\n56:  * resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\\n57:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t3p0</code>, <code>t3p1</code>. Each consumer is subscribed to all three topics.\\n58:  *\\n59:  * The assignment with both sticky and round robin assignors will be:\\n60:  * <ul>\\n61:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0]</code></li>\\n62:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t2p0, t3p1]</code></li>\\n63:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p0, t2p1]</code></li>\\n64:  * </ul>\\n65:  *\\n66:  * Now, let's assume <code>C1</code> is removed and a reassignment is about to happen. The round robin assignor would produce:\\n67:  * <ul>\\n68:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0, t2p0, t3p0]</code></li>\\n69:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p1, t1p1, t2p1, t3p1]</code></li>\\n70:  * </ul>\\n71:  *\\n72:  * while the sticky assignor would result in:\\n73:  * <ul>\\n74:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0, t2p0]</code></li>\\n75:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p1, t0p1, t3p1]</code></li>\\n76:  * </ul>\\n77:  * preserving all the previous assignments (unlike the round robin assignor).\\n78:  *</p>\\n79:  * <p><b>Example 2.</b> There are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\\n80:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions respectively.\\n81:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\\n82:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>. <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>; <code>C1</code> is subscribed to\\n83:  * <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>; and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * The round robin assignor would come up with the following assignment:\\n86:  * <ul>\\n87:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\\n88:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0]</code></li>\\n89:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n90:  * </ul>\\n91:  *\\n92:  * which is not as balanced as the assignment suggested by sticky assignor:\\n93:  * <ul>\\n94:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\\n95:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n96:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n97:  * </ul>\\n98:  *\\n99:  * Now, if consumer <code>C0</code> is removed, these two assignors would produce the following assignments.\\n100:  * Round Robin (preserves 3 partition assignments):\\n101:  * <ul>\\n102:  * <li><code>C1 [t0p0, t1p1]</code></li>\\n103:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n104:  * </ul>\\n105:  *\\n106:  * Sticky (preserves 5 partition assignments):\\n107:  * <ul>\\n108:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1, t0p0]</code></li>\\n109:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\\n110:  * </ul>\\n111:  *</p>\\n112:  * <h3>Impact on <code>ConsumerRebalanceListener</code></h3>\\n113:  * The sticky assignment strategy can provide some optimization to those consumers that have some partition cleanup code\\n114:  * in their <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code> callback listeners. The cleanup code is placed in that callback listener\\n115:  * because the consumer has no assumption or hope of preserving any of its assigned partitions after a rebalance when it\\n116:  * is using range or round robin assignor. The listener code would look like this:\\n117:  * <pre>\\n118:  * {@code\\n119:  * class TheOldRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n120:  *\\n121:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n122:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\\n123:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\\n124:  *       cleanupState(partition);\\n125:  *     }\\n126:  *   }\\n127:  *\\n128:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n129:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\\n130:  *       initializeState(partition);\\n131:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\\n132:  *     }\\n133:  *   }\\n134:  * }\\n135:  * }\\n136:  * </pre>\\n137:  *\\n138:  * As mentioned above, one advantage of the sticky assignor is that, in general, it reduces the number of partitions that\\n139:  * actually move from one consumer to another during a reassignment. Therefore, it allows consumers to do their cleanup\\n140:  * more efficiently. Of course, they still can perform the partition cleanup in the <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code>\\n141:  * listener, but they can be more efficient and make a note of their partitions before and after the rebalance, and do the\\n142:  * cleanup after the rebalance only on the partitions they have lost (which is normally not a lot). The code snippet below\\n143:  * clarifies this point:\\n144:  * <pre>\\n145:  * {@code\\n146:  * class TheNewRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n147:  *   Collection<TopicPartition> lastAssignment = Collections.emptyList();\\n148:  *\\n149:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n150:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n151:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\\n152:  *   }\\n153:  *\\n154:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> assignment) {\\n155:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(lastAssignment, assignment))\\n156:  *       cleanupState(partition);\\n157:  *\\n158:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(assignment, lastAssignment))\\n159:  *       initializeState(partition);\\n160:  *\\n161:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: assignment)\\n162:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\\n163:  *\\n164:  *     this.lastAssignment = assignment;\\n165:  *   }\\n166:  * }\\n167:  * }\\n168:  * </pre>\\n169:  *\\n170:  * Any consumer that uses sticky assignment can leverage this listener like this:\\n171:  * <code>consumer.subscribe(topics, new TheNewRebalanceListener());</code>\\n172:  *\\n173:  * Note that you can leverage the {@link CooperativeStickyAssignor} so that only partitions which are being\\n174:  * reassigned to another consumer will be revoked. Even though this may sound similar to\n46:  * how round robin assignor works, the second example below shows that it is not.\n47:  * During a reassignment it would perform the reassignment in such a way that in the new assignment\n48:  * <ol>\n49:  * <li>topic partitions are still distributed as evenly as possible, and</li>\n50:  * <li>topic partitions stay with their previously assigned consumers as much as possible.</li>\n51:  * </ol>\n52:  * Of course, the first goal above takes precedence over the second one.</p>\n53:  *\n54:  * <p><b>Example 1.</b> Suppose there are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n55:  * four topics <code>t0,</code> <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, <code>t3</code>, and each topic has 2 partitions,\n56:  * resulting in partitions <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t0p1</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\n57:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t3p0</code>, <code>t3p1</code>. Each consumer is subscribed to all three topics.\n58:  *\n59:  * The assignment with both sticky and round robin assignors will be:\n60:  * <ul>\n61:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0]</code></li>\n62:  * <li><code>C1: [t0p1, t2p0, t3p1]</code></li>\n63:  * <li><code>C2: [t1p0, t2p1]</code></li>\n64:  * </ul>\n65:  *\n66:  * Now, let's assume <code>C1</code> is removed and a reassignment is about to happen. The round robin assignor would produce:\n67:  * <ul>\n68:  * <li><code>C0: [t0p0, t1p0, t2p0, t3p0]</code></li>\n69:  * <li><code>C2: [t0p1, t1p1, t2p1, t3p1]</code></li>\n70:  * </ul>\n71:  *\n72:  * while the sticky assignor would result in:\n73:  * <ul>\n74:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0, t1p1, t3p0, t2p0]</code></li>\n75:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p1, t0p1, t3p1]</code></li>\n76:  * </ul>\n77:  * preserving all the previous assignments (unlike the round robin assignor).\n78:  *</p>\n79:  * <p><b>Example 2.</b> There are three consumers <code>C0</code>, <code>C1</code>, <code>C2</code>,\n80:  * and three topics <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>, with 1, 2, and 3 partitions respectively.\n81:  * Therefore, the partitions are <code>t0p0</code>, <code>t1p0</code>, <code>t1p1</code>, <code>t2p0</code>,\n82:  * <code>t2p1</code>, <code>t2p2</code>. <code>C0</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>; <code>C1</code> is subscribed to\n83:  * <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>; and <code>C2</code> is subscribed to <code>t0</code>, <code>t1</code>, <code>t2</code>.\n84:  *\n85:  * The round robin assignor would come up with the following assignment:\n86:  * <ul>\n87:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\n88:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0]</code></li>\n89:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p1, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n90:  * </ul>\n91:  *\n92:  * which is not as balanced as the assignment suggested by sticky assignor:\n93:  * <ul>\n94:  * <li><code>C0 [t0p0]</code></li>\n95:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1]</code></li>\n96:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n97:  * </ul>\n98:  *\n99:  * Now, if consumer <code>C0</code> is removed, these two assignors would produce the following assignments.\n100:  * Round Robin (preserves 3 partition assignments):\n101:  * <ul>\n102:  * <li><code>C1 [t0p0, t1p1]</code></li>\n103:  * <li><code>C2 [t1p0, t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n104:  * </ul>\n105:  *\n106:  * Sticky (preserves 5 partition assignments):\n107:  * <ul>\n108:  * <li><code>C1 [t1p0, t1p1, t0p0]</code></li>\n109:  * <li><code>C2 [t2p0, t2p1, t2p2]</code></li>\n110:  * </ul>\n111:  *</p>\n112:  * <h3>Impact on <code>ConsumerRebalanceListener</code></h3>\n113:  * The sticky assignment strategy can provide some optimization to those consumers that have some partition cleanup code\n114:  * in their <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code> callback listeners. The cleanup code is placed in that callback listener\n115:  * because the consumer has no assumption or hope of preserving any of its assigned partitions after a rebalance when it\n116:  * is using range or round robin assignor. The listener code would look like this:\n117:  * <pre>\n118:  * {@code\n119:  * class TheOldRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n120:  *\n121:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n122:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\n123:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\n124:  *       cleanupState(partition);\n125:  *     }\n126:  *   }\n127:  *\n128:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n129:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions) {\n130:  *       initializeState(partition);\n131:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\n132:  *     }\n133:  *   }\n134:  * }\n135:  * }\n136:  * </pre>\n137:  *\n138:  * As mentioned above, one advantage of the sticky assignor is that, in general, it reduces the number of partitions that\n139:  * actually move from one consumer to another during a reassignment. Therefore, it allows consumers to do their cleanup\n140:  * more efficiently. Of course, they still can perform the partition cleanup in the <code>onPartitionsRevoked()</code>\n141:  * listener, but they can be more efficient and make a note of their partitions before and after the rebalance, and do the\n142:  * cleanup after the rebalance only on the partitions they have lost (which is normally not a lot). The code snippet below\n143:  * clarifies this point:\n144:  * <pre>\n145:  * {@code\n146:  * class TheNewRebalanceListener implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n147:  *   Collection<TopicPartition> lastAssignment = Collections.emptyList();\n148:  *\n149:  *   void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n150:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: partitions)\n151:  *       commitOffsets(partition);\n152:  *   }\n153:  *\n154:  *   void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> assignment) {\n155:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(lastAssignment, assignment))\n156:  *       cleanupState(partition);\n157:  *\n158:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: difference(assignment, lastAssignment))\n159:  *       initializeState(partition);\n160:  *\n161:  *     for (TopicPartition partition: assignment)\n162:  *       initializeOffset(partition);\n163:  *\n164:  *     this.lastAssignment = assignment;\n165:  *   }\n166:  * }\n167:  * }\n168:  * </pre>\n169:  *\n170:  * Any consumer that uses sticky assignment can leverage this listener like this:\n171:  * <code>consumer.subscribe(topics, new TheNewRebalanceListener());</code>\n172:  *\n173:  * Note that you can leverage the {@link CooperativeStickyAssignor} so that only partitions which are being\n174:  * reassigned to another consumer will be revoked. That is the preferred assignor for newer cluster. See\n175:  * {@link ConsumerPartitionAssignor.RebalanceProtocol} for a detailed explanation of cooperative rebalancing.\n176:  */\n177: public class StickyAssignor extends AbstractStickyAssignor
